</p>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png/225px-Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png" decoding="async" width="225" height="32" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png/338px-Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png/450px-Something_Special_Pop_Smoke.png 2x" data-file-width="491" data-file-height="70" /></a></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Bashar Barakah Jackson</b> (July 20, 1999 – February 19, 2020), known professionally as <b>Pop Smoke</b>, was an American rapper. Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York City, Pop Smoke began his musical career in late 2018 with his debut single "MPR (Panic Part 3 Remix)". He rose to fame with the release of his breakout singles "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Party_(Pop_Smoke_song)" title="Welcome to the Party (Pop Smoke song)">Welcome to the Party</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dior_(song)" title="Dior (song)">Dior</a>" in 2019. He often collaborated with <a href="/wiki/UK_drill" title="UK drill">UK drill</a> artists and producers, who employed more minimal and aggressive instrumentation than <a href="/wiki/Drill_music" title="Drill music">American drill</a> artists from Chicago, reintroducing the sound as <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_drill" title="Brooklyn drill">Brooklyn drill</a>.
</p><p>Following his rise to fame, record producer <a href="/wiki/Rico_Beats" title="Rico Beats">Rico Beats</a> introduced Pop Smoke to <a href="/wiki/Steven_Victor" title="Steven Victor">Steven Victor</a> in April 2019. Victor would later have Pop Smoke sign a recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Victor_Victor_Worldwide" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Victor Worldwide">Victor Victor Worldwide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_Records" title="Republic Records">Republic Records</a>. He released his debut <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo" title="Meet the Woo">Meet the Woo</a></i> in July 2019. His second mixtape, <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo_2" title="Meet the Woo 2">Meet the Woo 2</a></i>, was released on February 7, 2020, and debuted at number seven on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i> Billboard</i> 200</a>, becoming the rapper's first top-10 project in the United States.
</p><p>Twelve days after the mixtape's release, Pop Smoke was murdered during a home invasion in Los Angeles. New York rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> was the executive producer of his posthumous debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Shoot_for_the_Stars,_Aim_for_the_Moon" title="Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon">Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon</a></i>, released on July 3, 2020. The album debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and all 19 tracks from the album were charted on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The album also spawned a string of international top-10 singles, including "<a href="/wiki/For_the_Night" title="For the Night">For the Night</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/DaBaby" title="DaBaby">DaBaby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil_Baby" title="Lil Baby">Lil Baby</a>) and "<a href="/wiki/What_You_Know_Bout_Love" title="What You Know Bout Love">What You Know Bout Love</a>". A year later, Republic Records released Pop Smoke's second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Faith_(Pop_Smoke_album)" title="Faith (Pop Smoke album)">Faith</a></i>, on July 16, 2021.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bashar Barakah Jackson was born on July 20, 1999, in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York City, to a Jamaican mother, Audrey Jackson, and a Panamanian father, Greg Jackson.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> He had an older brother named Obasi.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Jackson attended nine different schools while growing up in <a href="/wiki/Canarsie,_Brooklyn" title="Canarsie, Brooklyn">Canarsie, Brooklyn</a>. He played the African drums in his local church as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson was expelled from eighth grade for bringing a gun to school. He spent two years on house arrest after being charged with possessing a weapon.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Jackson started playing basketball as a point and shooting guard. He relocated to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> to enroll in Rocktop Academy. He was later forced to leave after being diagnosed with a <a href="/wiki/Heart_murmur" title="Heart murmur">heart murmur</a>, and Jackson eventually turned to street life.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In a <a href="/wiki/Genius_(website)" class="mw-redirect" title="Genius (website)">Genius</a> interview, he stated that his artist name of Pop Smoke is a combination of Poppa, a name given to him by his Panamanian grandmother, and Smocco Guwop, a nickname from childhood friends and it was also his old Instagram name.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He first attempted rapping during a 2018 visit to a Brooklyn recording studio with Jay Gwuapo. In late 2018, he was rapping over a beat from <a href="/wiki/808Melo" title="808Melo">808Melo</a>'s <i>YouTube</i> channel, Jackson recorded a track titled "MPR (Panic Part 3 Remix)" during the session.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> On January 28, 2019, he released "Flexin'".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, Jackson befriended producer <a href="/wiki/Rico_Beats" title="Rico Beats">Rico Beats</a>, who was acquainted with record executive <a href="/wiki/Steven_Victor" title="Steven Victor">Steven Victor</a>.
</p><p>The three set up an interview, and in April 2019, Jackson signed to <a href="/wiki/Steven_Victor#Victor_Victor_Worldwide" title="Steven Victor">Victor Victor Worldwide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic_Records" title="Republic Records">Republic Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-comp_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> On April 23, 2019, Jackson released his breakout single, "<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Party_(Pop_Smoke_song)" title="Welcome to the Party (Pop Smoke song)">Welcome to the Party</a>", that was produced by 808Melo.<sup id="cite_ref-all_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-all-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Many remixes of the song were later recorded, with the commercially released versions featuring <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and the other featuring <a href="/wiki/Skepta" title="Skepta">Skepta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-all_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-all-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Jackson released his debut mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo" title="Meet the Woo">Meet the Woo</a></i> on July 26, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> From October to December 2019, Jackson released multiple singles, including "<a href="/wiki/War_(Pop_Smoke_song)" title="War (Pop Smoke song)">War</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Lil_Tjay" title="Lil Tjay">Lil Tjay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and "100k on a Coupe" with <a href="/wiki/Calboy" title="Calboy">Calboy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 27, 2019, Jackson appeared on <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Cactus_Jack_Records" title="Cactus Jack Records">Cactus Jack Records</a> compilation album <i><a href="/wiki/JackBoys" title="JackBoys">JackBoys</a></i> on the song "<a href="/wiki/Gatti_(song)" title="Gatti (song)">Gatti</a>" which was also accompanied by a music video.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> "Gatti" debuted and peaked at number 69 on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, giving Jackson his first and only Hot 100 appearance before his death.<sup id="cite_ref-bill5_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill5-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> On January 16, 2020, Jackson released "<a href="/wiki/Christopher_Walking" title="Christopher Walking">Christopher Walking</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On February 7, 2020, twelve days before his death, Jackson released his second mixtape <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo_2" title="Meet the Woo 2">Meet the Woo 2</a></i>, with features from <a href="/wiki/Quavo" title="Quavo">Quavo</a>, <a href="/wiki/A_Boogie_wit_da_Hoodie" title="A Boogie wit da Hoodie">A Boogie wit da Hoodie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fivio_Foreign" title="Fivio Foreign">Fivio Foreign</a> and Lil Tjay.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The mixtape debuted at number seven on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, earning Jackson his first top-10 hit in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Five days after its release, a deluxe edition was released with three new songs, each featuring a guest appearance, consisting of <a href="/wiki/Nav_(rapper)" title="Nav (rapper)">Nav</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gunna_(rapper)" title="Gunna (rapper)">Gunna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PnB_Rock" title="PnB Rock">PnB Rock</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Jackson teased to social media his debut headlining concert tour <a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Meet the Woo Tour">Meet the Woo Tour</a> to promote both his mixtapes.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hiphop_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphop-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The tour was planned to begin in the US in March, and end in the UK in April.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphop_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphop-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Posthumous_releases">Posthumous releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Posthumous releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Dior_(song)" title="Dior (song)">Dior</a>", the second single off <i>Meet the Woo</i>, became Jackson's first posthumous solo hit, peaking at number 22 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and number 33 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bill5_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill5-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bill10_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill10-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of March 2020, American rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> announced on his <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> that he had decided to executive produce and finish Jackson's debut studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bill_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> After his announcement, 50 Cent called artists like <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Ricch" title="Roddy Ricch">Roddy Ricch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drake_(musician)" title="Drake (musician)">Drake</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown" title="Chris Brown">Chris Brown</a> wanting to feature them on the record.<sup id="cite_ref-xxl_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxl-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bill_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Pop Smoke had wanted to take his mother to an awards show prompting 50 Cent to promise to take her to one when the album was complete.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 16, 2020, a documentary on Pop Smoke's life was announced to be in the works.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> On May 14, 2020, Victor announced that Pop Smoke's debut studio album would be posthumously released on June 12, 2020. The album was named <i><a href="/wiki/Shoot_for_the_Stars,_Aim_for_the_Moon" title="Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon">Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> It was originally set for release on June 12, 2020, but was pushed back out of respect for the <a href="/wiki/George_Floyd" title="George Floyd">George Floyd</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Floyd_protests" title="George Floyd protests">protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Instead, on the album's original release date, the lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Make_It_Rain_(Pop_Smoke_song)" title="Make It Rain (Pop Smoke song)">Make It Rain</a>", featuring fellow <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a> rapper <a href="/wiki/Rowdy_Rebel" title="Rowdy Rebel">Rowdy Rebel</a> was released.<sup id="cite_ref-pitch3_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitch3-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rebel's verse was recorded through a <a href="/wiki/Collect_call" title="Collect call">collect call</a> since he was incarcerated at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-pitch3_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pitch3-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Virgil_Abloh" title="Virgil Abloh">Virgil Abloh</a> created the album's original artwork.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The cover artwork provoked significant criticism from fans who called it "lazy" and "rushed" and felt it was disrespectful. It prompted a <a href="/wiki/Change.org" title="Change.org">Change.org</a> petition attracting tens of thousands of signatures.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ryder_Ripps" title="Ryder Ripps">Ryder Ripps</a> created the final cover art with the chrome rose against a black background. Jackson's mother chose the final album cover hours before the album was released commercially.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album was officially released on July 3, 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> to commercial success, reaching number one in several countries, including on the <i>Billboard</i> 200.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> All 19 songs on the album charted on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100,<sup id="cite_ref-bill10_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bill10-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> with "<a href="/wiki/For_the_Night" title="For the Night">For the Night</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Lil_Baby" title="Lil Baby">Lil Baby</a> and <a href="/wiki/DaBaby" title="DaBaby">DaBaby</a>, debuting and peaking at number six, giving Pop Smoke his first top-10 hit in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On July 20, 2020, which what would have been Jackson's 21st birthday, a deluxe edition of the album was released, and featured 15 new additional tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's fifth single "<a href="/wiki/What_You_Know_Bout_Love" title="What You Know Bout Love">What You Know Bout Love</a>", ended up peaking at number nine on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, giving Pop Smoke his second top-10 hit in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> On February 26, 2021, "<a href="/wiki/AP_(song)" title="AP (song)">AP</a>" was released as the lead single for the <i><a href="/wiki/Boogie_(2021_film)" title="Boogie (2021 film)">Boogie</a></i> soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Pop Smoke was cast as Monk in a minor role for <i>Boogie</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Without assistance from 50 Cent, a second posthumous album titled <i><a href="/wiki/Faith_(Pop_Smoke_album)" title="Faith (Pop Smoke album)">Faith</a></i> was released on July 16, 2021, to mixed reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allhiphop1_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allhiphop1-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number one on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, making Pop Smoke the first artist to have their first two posthumous albums debut at the top of the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-allhiphop1_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allhiphop1-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> A deluxe version, featuring four additional tracks, was released on July 20, 2021, which what would have been Jackson's 22nd birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Six more tracks were added on July 30.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On January 17, 2020, after returning from <a href="/wiki/Paris_Fashion_Week" title="Paris Fashion Week">Paris Fashion Week</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-:2_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Jackson was arrested by federal authorities at <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a> after stealing a <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Wraith_(2013)" title="Rolls-Royce Wraith (2013)">Rolls-Royce Wraith</a>, valued at $375,000, whose owner reported it stolen after Jackson had reportedly borrowed it in California for a music video shoot on the condition it would be returned the next day. Investigators believed he arranged for the car to be transported on a flatbed truck to New York. He posted a photo of himself in front of the stolen car on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> and Facebook. The car was recovered by authorities at Jackson's mother's house, in the <a href="/wiki/Canarsie,_Brooklyn" title="Canarsie, Brooklyn">Canarsie</a> section of <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-comp3_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp3-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After his arrest, police questioned him about a non-fatal shooting that took place in Brooklyn in June 2019. The police thought he had information on the shooting because they claimed to have footage of him driving a car in reverse near the scene of the crime.<sup id="cite_ref-comp3_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp3-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The police also tried to pressure Jackson into telling them more information about the Crips, GS9, and other Brooklyn street gangs, but he refused to talk.<sup id="cite_ref-comp3_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp3-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was charged with grand theft auto, posted a $250,000 bond, and agreed to stay away from known gang members and submit drug tests to the US pretrial services.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The conditions Jackson was put under hindered some of his performances like the "BK Drip Concert" at Kings Theatre in Flatbush in February 2020, as gang members were in the audience.<sup id="cite_ref-comp3_47-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp3-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Murder">Murder</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Murder">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox vevent"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above summary" style="font-size:125%;">Murder of Pop Smoke</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png/220px-Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png/330px-Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png/440px-Map_of_the_Hollywood_Hills_district_of_Los_Angeles.png 2x" data-file-width="827" data-file-height="615" /></a></span><div class="infobox-caption">Map of the Hollywood Hills neighborhood of Los Angeles</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Location</th><td class="infobox-data location"><a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Hills" title="Hollywood Hills">Hollywood Hills</a>, Los Angeles, California</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Date</th><td class="infobox-data">February&#160;19, 2020<span class="noprint">&#59;&#32;3 years ago</span><span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2020-02-19</span>)</span> <br /><abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 4:30 a.m.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Pacific_Time_Zone" title="Pacific Time Zone">PST</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Target</th><td class="infobox-data">Bashar Barakah Jackson, <abbr title="also known as">a.k.a.</abbr>&#160;Pop Smoke</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Attack type</div></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">Murder</a> by <a href="/wiki/Gun_violence_in_the_United_States" title="Gun violence in the United States">shooting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_invasion" title="Home invasion">home invasion</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Deaths</th><td class="infobox-data">1 (Bashar Barakah Jackson, <abbr title="also known as">a.k.a.</abbr>&#160;Pop Smoke)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Motive</th><td class="infobox-data">Under investigation</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Accused</th><td class="infobox-data"><b>Shooter:</b><br />Unnamed 15-year old<br /><b>Accomplices:</b><br /><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li>Jaquan Murphy</li>
<li>Keandre D. Rodgers</li>
<li>Corey Walker</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Convicted</th><td class="infobox-data"><b>Convicted as an accomplice:</b><br />Unnamed 17-year old</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Verdict</th><td class="infobox-data"><b>17-year old:</b><br /><a href="/wiki/Pleaded_guilty" class="mw-redirect" title="Pleaded guilty">Pleaded guilty</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Convictions</th><td class="infobox-data"><b>17-year old:</b><br /><a href="/wiki/Voluntary_manslaughter" title="Voluntary manslaughter">Voluntary manslaughter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_invasion" title="Home invasion">home invasion</a> <a href="/wiki/Robbery" title="Robbery">robbery</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Charges</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Murder_in_California_law" title="Murder in California law">First degree murder</a> with <a href="/wiki/Special_circumstances_(criminal_law)" title="Special circumstances (criminal law)">special circumstances</a><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><br /></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Sentence</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align: left;"><b>17-year old:</b><br />4 years and 2 months in <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_detention" class="mw-redirect" title="Juvenile detention">juvenile detention</a><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>On February 19, 2020, Jackson was renting a house through <a href="/wiki/Airbnb" title="Airbnb">Airbnb</a> owned by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Real_Housewives" title="The Real Housewives">The Real Housewives</a></i> star <a href="/wiki/Teddi_Mellencamp" class="mw-redirect" title="Teddi Mellencamp">Teddi Mellencamp</a> and her husband, Edwin Arroyave, in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Hills" title="Hollywood Hills">Hollywood Hills</a>, California.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nydn3_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn3-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> At around 4:30&#160;a.m., five hooded men, including one wearing a ski mask and carrying a handgun, broke into the house through a second-story balcony.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vibe_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The intruders held a gun to a woman's head and threatened to kill her.<sup id="cite_ref-complex21_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex21-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nydn3_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn3-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Shortly thereafter, the woman heard the men shoot Jackson three times after an altercation.<sup id="cite_ref-nydn3_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn3-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Police_Department" title="Los Angeles Police Department">LAPD</a> received news of the home invasion from a call from the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-new2_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new2-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Police arrived at the home six minutes later and found Jackson with multiple gunshot wounds.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> He was rushed to <a href="/wiki/Cedars-Sinai_Medical_Center" title="Cedars-Sinai Medical Center">Cedars-Sinai Medical Center</a>, where doctors performed a <a href="/wiki/Thoracotomy" title="Thoracotomy">thoracotomy</a> on the left side of his chest.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> A few hours later, he was pronounced dead.<sup id="cite_ref-vul_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vul-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> He was 20 years old. On February 21, the Los Angeles County Department of Medical Examiner-Coroner revealed that the cause of Jackson's death was a gunshot wound to the chest.<sup id="cite_ref-lat_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The LAPD at first suspected that Jackson's death was gang-related, as he was tied to the <a href="/wiki/Crips" title="Crips">Crips</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vul_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vul-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> However, the LAPD later believed his death was the consequence of a home robbery gone wrong.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> It was believed the intruders stole Jackson's gold watch and other jewelry before running away from the house.<sup id="cite_ref-complex21_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex21-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In May 2021, a 15-year-old, the youngest of the four intruders, allegedly admitted to killing Jackson over a diamond-studded <a href="/wiki/Rolex" title="Rolex">Rolex</a> during a recorded interview with a cellmate at a juvenile detention center.<sup id="cite_ref-nydn2_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn2-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The 15-year-old told the cellmate that Jackson at first complied with their requests for jewelry but then tried to fight them, and a confrontation broke out in which Jackson was <a href="/wiki/Pistol-whipping" title="Pistol-whipping">pistol-whipped</a> and shot with a <a href="/wiki/Beretta_M92" class="mw-redirect" title="Beretta M92">Beretta M92</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beast_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beast-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The intruders made off with his Rolex, which they sold for $2,000.<sup id="cite_ref-nydn2_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn2-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-beast_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beast-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The day before his murder, Jackson and friend Michael Durodola<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> posted several images on social media, including one in which Mellencamp's home address can be seen in the background.<sup id="cite_ref-vul_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vul-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The rapper also posted a story on Instagram and Facebook of gifts he had received.<sup id="cite_ref-vul_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vul-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> One showed the house's full address on the packaging, giving out its location.<sup id="cite_ref-vul_62-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vul-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson's body was originally planned to be buried at the <a href="/wiki/Cypress_Hills_Cemetery" title="Cypress Hills Cemetery">Cypress Hills Cemetery</a> but was later changed to <a href="/wiki/Green-Wood_Cemetery" title="Green-Wood Cemetery">Green-Wood Cemetery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Family, friends, and fans of Jackson gathered in his hometown of Canarsie, Brooklyn, to show their respects.<sup id="cite_ref-e_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> His casket was pulled in a horse-drawn carriage and was surrounded by glass windows and white curtains.<sup id="cite_ref-e_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> On September 11, 2021, it was discovered that his grave site was vandalized, with the headstone smashed.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 9, 2020, three adult men and two minors were arrested for the murder of the rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> One of the adult suspects has been charged with murder with a special circumstance that alleged the killing was committed "during the commission of a robbery and a burglary", and another charged with attempted murder.<sup id="cite_ref-new4_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new4-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbs_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The two juveniles were charged with murder and robbery in juvenile court. As California law requires a minor to be at least 16 at the time of the crime, the 15-year-old could not be tried as an adult; and, under <a href="/wiki/George_Gasc%C3%B3n" title="George Gascón">George Gascón</a>'s policy to keep all juveniles in juvenile court,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="The policy needs to be referenced and a first name and position should be provided (June 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> the 17-year-old could not be tried as an adult, either.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-new4_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-new4-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remembrance">Remembrance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Remembrance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jackson's parents, Audrey and Greg Jackson, shared memories of their son before saying how gun violence took him away from them.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>On February 19th, at 4:00 AM, a gun was used to take my son from me. You know him as Pop Smoke, we called him 'Shar'. Because of gun violence, I'll never see my son run up the front of our steps, taking them two at a time; he won't ever take my hands again and dance with me; he won't come into my room and muscle pose in the mirror. Gun violence destroys families. It must stop.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="templatequotecite">—&#8202;<cite>Audrey Jackson during a "Gun Violence Destroys Families" public service announcement</cite></div></blockquote>
<p>Danny Schwartz wrote in <a href="/wiki/The_Ringer_(website)" title="The Ringer (website)">The Ringer</a> that "Pop Smoke conquered New York rap and gave the city the kind of readymade and potentially defining star it hadn't seen in years". He claimed that "in New York City city, '<a href="/wiki/Welcome_to_the_Party_(Pop_Smoke_song)" title="Welcome to the Party (Pop Smoke song)">Welcome to the Party</a>' was more omnipresent than hits like '<a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Road" title="Old Town Road">Old Town Road</a>'."<sup id="cite_ref-ring_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ring-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jackson's work ethic was widely praised by his peers in the music industry. The executive producer of his posthumous album, 50 Cent, revealed Smoke was always "writing what [50] said down" on his telephone, while <a href="/wiki/Quavo" title="Quavo">Quavo</a> added he "felt like [he] was talking to somebody that had been in the game for three years already".<sup id="cite_ref-lastdays_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lastdays-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Producer <a href="/wiki/Rico_Beats" title="Rico Beats">Rico Beats</a> stated that, in his last few months, Jackson started "telling kids, don't go the gang route", wanting to "be a better person".<sup id="cite_ref-lastdays_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lastdays-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A few months after his death, his family announced the creation of Shoot for the Stars, a foundation Jackson had planned to create prior to his death, with the goal of helping and inspiring inner-city youth.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> After his death, several murals of him were created in <a href="/wiki/Canarsie" class="mw-redirect" title="Canarsie">Canarsie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-liveagain_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liveagain-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>  Although his lyrics do not generally contend with <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a> or racism, his songs, particularly "<a href="/wiki/Dior_(song)" title="Dior (song)">Dior</a>", were popularly used during the <a href="/wiki/George_Floyd_protests" title="George Floyd protests">George Floyd protests</a> in New York City as a symbol of resistance.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-liveagain_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liveagain-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Meet_the_Woo_Tour">Meet the Woo Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pop_Smoke&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Meet the Woo Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox vevent"><caption class="infobox-title summary">Meet the Woo Tour</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader" style="font-weight: bold;"><span class="category">Tour</span> by <span class="attendee">Pop Smoke</span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Meetthewootour.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/82/Meetthewootour.png/270px-Meetthewootour.png" decoding="async" width="270" height="180" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/82/Meetthewootour.png 1.5x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="258" /></a></span><div class="infobox-caption">Poster for the tour</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Associated album</th><td class="infobox-data"><i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo" title="Meet the Woo">Meet the Woo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo_2" title="Meet the Woo 2">Meet the Woo 2</a></i></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Start date</th><td class="infobox-data">March 2, 2020</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">End date</th><td class="infobox-data">April 16, 2020</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label"><abbr title="Number">No.</abbr> of shows</th><td class="infobox-data">25</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Meet the Woo Tour</b> was scheduled to be the debut headlining concert tour by Pop Smoke. It was launched in support of his two mixtapes, <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo" title="Meet the Woo">Meet the Woo</a></i> (2019) and <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Woo_2" title="Meet the Woo 2">Meet the Woo 2</a></i> (2020), and had been set to consist of concerts in North America and the United Kingdom. The tour was announced in January 2020, with dates being released at the same time. Pop Smoke later added more UK tour dates after high demand from fans.
</p><p>Tour dates were released on the same day for North America,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> while dates for the United Kingdom were revealed in February.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Due to high demand from fans, more tour dates for the UK were revealed on February 13, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-twitter_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitter-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Pop Smoke shared a promotional flyer for the tour on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-def_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-def-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Pop Smoke and his team were planning on finishing, mixing, and mastering his debut studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Shoot_for_the_Stars,_Aim_for_the_Moon" title="Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon">Shoot for the Stars, Aim for the Moon</a></i>, starting the first week of March 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-comp_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comp-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Revolt_(TV_network)" title="Revolt (TV network)">Revolt</a>, Pop Smoke's DJ Jeffrey Archer talked about the tour. "Honestly, it's nothing planned yet. We just got those dates. This is officially going to be our first real big tour. This is going to be a month. I'm very excited about it. We're going to a few places we've never been to. We've been getting feedback over the last seven months [from] fans like, 'Please come out here.' There are loyal fans at these shows. You should expect a lot more music and shows. He has a lot of music coming out with a lot of artists. He's not playing. We're definitely shaking the room in 2020."<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The tour was canceled after Pop Smoke was shot and killed. Fans were offered refunds after Pop Smoke's death: "As we mourn the loss of this great artist, refunds will be available at point of purchase."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
